      <span class="s3">45</span></p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><ol id="l7"><li data-list-text="1)"><h2 style="padding-left: 21pt;text-indent: -14pt;text-align: left;">what are static blocks and static initalizers in Java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Static blocks or static initializers are used to initalize static fields in java. we declare static blocks when we want to intialize static fields in our class. Static blocks gets executed exactly once when the class is loaded</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">. Static blocks are executed even before the constructors are executed.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><h2 style="padding-left: 24pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">How to call one constructor from the other constructor ?</h2></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">With in the same class if we want to call one constructor from other we use this() method. Based on the number of parameters we pass appropriate this() method is called.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Restrictions for using this method :</p><ol id="l8"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">this must be the first statement in the constructor</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 16pt;text-indent: -9pt;text-align: left;">we cannot use two this() methods in the constructor</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><h2 style="padding-left: 27pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">What is method overriding in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">If we have methods with same signature (same name, same signature, same return type) in super class and subclass then we say</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">subclass method is overridden by superclass. When to use overriding in java</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If we want same method with different behaviour in superclass and subclass then we go for overriding. When we call overridden method with subclass reference subclass method is called hiding the superclass method.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><h2 style="padding-left: 21pt;text-indent: -14pt;text-align: left;">What is super keyword in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Variables and methods of super class can be overridden in subclass . In case of overriding , a subclass object call its own variables and methods. Subclass cannot access the variables and methods of superclass because the overridden variables or methods hides the methods and variables of super class. But still <span class="s4">java </span>provides a way to access super class members even if its members are overridden. Super is used to access superclass variables, methods, constructors.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Super can be used in two forms :</p><ol id="l9"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">First form is for calling super class constructor.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Second one is to call super class variables,methods. Super if present must be the first statement.</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><h2 style="padding-left: 24pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">Difference between method overloading and method overriding in java ?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s5" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method Overloading</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s5" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method Overriding</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">1) Method Overloading occurs with in the same class</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method Overriding occurs between</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">two   classes superclass and subclass</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">2) Since it involves with only one class inheritance is not involved.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Since method overriding occurs between superclass and subclass inheritance is involved.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">3)In overloading return type need not be the same</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">3) In overriding return type must be same.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">4) Parameters must be different when we do overloading</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">4) Parameters must be same.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 3pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5) Static polymorphism can be acheived using method overloading</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 3pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5) Dynamic polymorphism can be acheived using method overriding.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">6) In overloading one method can’t hide the another</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">6) In overriding subclass method hides that of the superclass method.</p></td></tr></table></li><li data-list-text="6)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 24pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">Difference between abstract class and interface ?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s7" style="padding-left: 57pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Interface</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s7" style="padding-left: 48pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Abstract Class</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">1)  Interface contains only abstract methods</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">1) Abstract class can contain abstract methods, concrete methods or both</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 15pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">2) Access Specifiers for methods in interface must be public</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">2) Except private we can have any access specifier for methods in abstract class.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 15pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">3)  Variables defined must be public , static , final</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">3) Except private variables can have any access specifiers</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">4) Multiple Inheritance in <span class="s8">java </span>is implemented using interface</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">4)We cannot achieve multiple inheritance using abstract class.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 15pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5) To implement an interface we use implements keyword</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5)To implement an interface we use implements keyword</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="7)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">Why java is platform independent?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">The most unique feature of java is platform independent. In any programming language soruce code is compiled in to executable code . This cannot be run across all platforms. When javac compiles a java program it generates an executable file called .class file.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">class file contains byte codes. Byte codes are interpreted only by JVM’s . Since these JVM’s are made available across all platforms by Sun Microsystems, we can execute this byte code in any platform. Byte code generated in windows environment can also be executed in linux environment. This makes java platform independent.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="8)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: justify;">What is method overloading in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: justify;">A class having two or more methods with same name but with different arguments then we say that those methods are overloaded. Static polymorphism is achieved in java using method overloading.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">Method overloading is used when we want the methods to perform similar tasks but with different inputs or values. When an overloaded method is invoked java first checks the method name, and the number of arguments ,type of arguments; based on this compiler executes this method.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">Compiler decides which method to call at compile time. By using overloading static polymorphism or static binding can be achieved in java.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: justify;">Note : Return type is not part of method signature. we may have methods with different return types but return type alone is not sufficient to call a method in java.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="9)"><h2 style="padding-bottom: 1pt;padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: justify;">What is difference between c++ and Java ?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s7" style="padding-left: 60pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s7" style="padding-left: 41pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">C++</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">1)  Java is platform independent</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">C++ is platform dependent.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">2)  There are no pointers in java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">There are pointers in C++.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">3)  There is no operator overloading in java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">C ++ has operator overloading.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">4)  There is garbage collection in java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">There is no garbage collection</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">5)  Supports multithreading</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Does’nt support multithreading</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">6)  There are no templates in java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">There are templates in java</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">7)  There are no global variables in java</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">There are global variables in c++</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="10)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">What is JIT compiler ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">JIT compiler stands for Just in time compiler. JIT compiler compiles byte code in to executable code . JIT a part of JVM .JIT cannot convert complete java program in to executable code it converts as and when it is needed during execution.</p></li><li data-list-text="11)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">What is bytecode in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">When a javac compiler compiler compiles a class it generates .class file. This .class file contains set of instructions called byte code. Byte code is a machine independent language and contains set of instructions which are to be executed only by JVM. JVM can understand this byte codes.</p></li><li data-list-text="12)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 46pt;text-indent: -39pt;text-align: left;">Difference between this() and super() in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">this() is used to access one constructor from another with in the same class while super() is used to access superclass constructor. Either this() or super() exists it must be the first statement in the constructor.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="13)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">What is a class ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Classes are fundamental or basic unit in Object Oriented Programming .A class is kind of blueprint or template for objects. Class defines variables, methods. A class tells what type of objects we are creating. For example take Department class tells us we can create department type objects. We can create any number of department objects.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">All programming constructs in <span class="s4">java </span>reside in class. When JVM starts running it first looks for the class when we compile. Every Java application must have atleast one class and one main method.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Class starts with class keyword. A class definition must be saved in class file that has same as class name. File name must end with .java extension.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s12" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public class <span class="p">FirstClass</span></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{<b>public static void </b>main(String[] args)</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{System.<i>out</i>.println(“My First class”);</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 10pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If we see the above class when we compile JVM loads the FirstClass and generates a .class file(FirstClass.class). When we run the program we are running the class and then executes the main method.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="14)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">What is an object ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">An Object is instance of class. A class defines type of object. Each object belongs to some class.Every object contains state and behavior. State is determined by value of attributes and behavior is called method. Objects are alos called as an instance.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">To instantiate the class we declare with the class type.</p><p class="s12" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public class<span class="p">FirstClass {</span>public static void<span class="p">main(String[] args)</span></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">FirstClass f=new FirstClass(); System.<i>out</i>.println(“My First class”);</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">To instantiate the FirstClass we use this statement FirstClass f=new FirstClass();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">f is used to refer FirstClass object.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="15)"><h2 style="padding-left: 24pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">What is method in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">It contains the executable body that can be applied to the specific object of the class.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method includes method name, parameters or arguments and return type and a body of executable code.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Syntax : type methodName(Argument List){</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">ex : public float add(int a, int b, int c)</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">methods can have multiple arguments. Separate with commas when we have multiple arguments.</p></li><li data-list-text="16)"><h2 style="padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">What is encapsulation ?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 3pt;text-align: left;"><span style=" color: #F0F; font-family:Verdana, sans-serif; font-style: italic; font-weight: normal; text-decoration: none; font-size: 8.5pt;">The process of wrapping or putting up of data in to a single unit class and keeps data safe from misuse is called encapsulation .</span></p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Through encapsulation we can hide and protect the data stored in <span class="s4">java </span>objects.Java supports encapsulation through access control. There are four access control modifiers in java public , private</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">,protected and default level.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">For example take a car class , In car we have many parts which is not required for driver to know what all it consists inside. He is required to know only about how to start and stop the car. So we can expose what all are required and hide the rest by using encapsulation.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="17)"><h2 style="padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">Why main() method is public, static and void in java ?</h2><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s10" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;"><u>public :</u> <span style=" color: #000;">“public” is an access specifier which can be used outside the class. When main method is declared public it means it can be used outside class.</span></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;"><span class="s9">static : </span>To call a method we require object. Sometimes it may be required to call a method without the help of object. Then we declare that method as static. JVM calls the main() method without creating object by declaring keyword static.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;"><span class="s9"> void : </span>void return type is used when a method does’nt return any value . main() method does’nt return any value, so main() is declared as void.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Signature : public static void main(String[] args) {</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="18)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">Explain about main() method in java ?</h2><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Main() method is starting point of execution for all java applications.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public static void main(String[] args) {}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">String args[] are array of string objects we need to pass from command line arguments. Every Java application must have atleast one main method.</p></li><li data-list-text="19)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 27pt;text-indent: -17pt;text-align: left;">What is constructor in java ?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span style=" color: #F0F; font-family:Verdana, sans-serif; font-style: italic; font-weight: normal; text-decoration: none; font-size: 8.5pt;">A constructor is a special method used to initialize objects in java.</span></p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">we use constructors to initialize all variables in the class when an object is created. As and when an object is created it is initialized automatically with the help of constructor in java.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">We have two types of constructors Default Constructor</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Parameterized Constructor Signature : public classname()</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Signature : public classname(parameters list)</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="20)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">What is difference between length and length() method in java ?</h2><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p class="s10" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 3pt;text-align: left;"><u>length() : </u> <span style=" color: #000;">In String class we have length() method which is used to return the number of characters in string.</span></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex : String str = “Hello World”; System.out.println(str.length());</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Str.length() will return 11 characters including space.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;"><span class="s9">length : </span>we have length instance variable in arrays which will return the number of values or objects in array.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">For example :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">String days[]={” Sun”,”Mon”,”wed”,”thu”,”fri”,”sat”};</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Will return 6 since the number of values in days array is 6.</p></li><li data-list-text="21)"><h2 style="padding-left: 46pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">What is ASCII Code?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">ASCII stands for American Standard code for Information Interchange. ASCII character range is 0 to 255. We can’t add more characters to the ASCII Character set. ASCII character set supports only English. That</p><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">is the reason, if we see C language we can write c language only in English we can’t write in other languages because it uses ASCII code.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="22)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">What is Unicode ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Unicode is a character set developed by Unicode Consortium. To support all languages in the world <span class="s4">Java</span> supports Unicode values. Unicode characters were represented by 16 bits and its character range is 0- 65,535.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Java uses ASCII code for all input elements except for Strings,identifiers, and comments. If we want to use telugu we can use telugu characters for identifiers.We can enter comments in telugu.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="23)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">Difference between Character Constant and String Constant in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Character constant is enclosed in single quotes. String constants are enclosed in double quotes. Character constants are single digit or character. String Constants are collection of characters.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex :’2’, ‘A’</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex : “Hello World”</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="24)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">What are constants and how to create constants in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Constants are fixed values whose values cannot be changed during the execution of program. We create constants in java using final keyword.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Ex : final int number =10;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">final String str=”java-interview –questions”</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="25)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">Difference between ‘&gt;&gt;’ and ‘&gt;&gt;&gt;’ operators in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">&gt;&gt; is a right shift operator shifts all of the bits in a value to the right to a specified number of times. int a =15;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">a= a &gt;&gt; 3;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The above line of code moves 15 three characters right.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">&gt;&gt;&gt; is an unsigned shift operator used to shift right. The places which were vacated by shift are filled with zeroes.</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Core java Interview questions on Coding Standards</p></li><li data-list-text="26)"><h2 style="padding-left: 39pt;text-indent: -32pt;text-align: left;">Explain Java Coding Standards for classes or Java coding conventions for classes?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Sun has created Java Coding standards or Java Coding Conventions . It is recommended highly to follow java coding standards.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Classnames should start with uppercase letter. Classnames names should be nouns. If Class name is of multiple words then the first letter of inner word must be capital letter.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Ex : Employee, EmployeeDetails, ArrayList, TreeSet, HashSet</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="27)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">Explain Java Coding standards for interfaces?</h2><ol id="l10"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Interface should start with uppercase letters</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Interfaces names should be adjectives Example : Runnable, Serializable, Marker, Cloneable</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="28)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">Explain Java Coding standards for Methods?</h2><ol id="l11"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Method names should start with small letters.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Method names are usually verbs</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">If method contains multiple words, every inner word should start with uppercase letter. Ex : toString()</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Method name must be combination of verb and noun Ex : getCarName(),getCarNumber()</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="29)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">Explain Java Coding Standards for variables ?</h2><ol id="l12"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Variable names should start with small letters.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Variable names should be nouns</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Short meaningful names are recommended.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">If there are multiple words every innerword should start with Uppecase character. Ex : string,value,empName,empSalary</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="30)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">Explain Java Coding Standards for Constants?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Constants in java are created using static and final keywords.</p><ol id="l13"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Constants contains only uppercase letters.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">If constant name is combination of two words it should be separated by underscore.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: justify;">Constant names are usually nouns.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">Ex:MAX_VALUE, MIN_VALUE, MAX_PRIORITY, MIN_PRIORITY</p></li><li data-list-text="31)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: justify;">Difference between overriding and overloading in java?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Overriding</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Overloading</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">In overriding method names must be same</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">In overloading method names must be same</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Argument List must be same</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Argument list must be different atleast order of arguments.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Return type can be same or we can return covariant type. From 1.5 covariant types are allowed</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Return type can be different in overloading.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">We cant increase the level of checked exceptions. No restrictions for unchecked exceptions</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In overloading different exceptions can be thrown.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A method can only be overridden in subclass</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">A method can be overloaded in same class or subclass</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Private,static and final variables cannot be overridden.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Private , static and final variables can be overloaded.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 11pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: justify;">In overriding which method is called is decided at runtime based on the type of object referenced at run time</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In overloading which method to call is decided at compile time based on reference type.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Overriding is also known as Runtime polymorphism, dynamic polymorphism or late binding</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Overloading is also known as Compile time polymorphism, static polymorphism or early binding.</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="32)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: justify;">What is ‘IS-A ‘ relationship in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">‘is a’ relationship is also known as inheritance. We can implement ‘is a’ relationship or inheritance in <span class="s4">java</span> using extends keyword. The advantage or inheritance or is a relationship is reusability of code instead of duplicating the code.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">Ex : Motor cycle is a vehicle</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">Car is a vehicle Both car and motorcycle extends vehicle.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="33)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">What is ‘HAS A’’ relationship in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">‘Has a ‘ relationship is also known as “composition or Aggregation”. As in inheritance we have ‘extends’ keyword we don’t have any keyword to implement ‘Has a’ relationship in java. The main advantage of ‘Has-A‘ relationship in java code reusability.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="34)"><h2 style="padding-bottom: 1pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;text-align: left;">Difference between ‘IS-A’ and ‘HAS-A’ relationship in java?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">IS-A relationship</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">HAS- A RELATIONSHIP</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Is a relationship also known as inheritance</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Has a relationship also known as composition or aggregation.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For IS-A relationship we uses extends keyword</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For Has a relationship we use new keyword</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex : Car is a vehicle.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Ex : Car has an engine. We cannot say Car is an engine</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">The main advantage of inheritance is reusability of code</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">The main advantage of has a relationship is reusability of code.</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="35)"><h2 style="padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">Explain about instanceof operator in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Instanceof operator is used to test the object is of which type. Syntax : &lt;reference expression&gt; instanceof &lt;destination type&gt;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Instanceof returns true if reference expression is subtype of destination type. Instanceof returns false if reference expression is null.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Example : <b>public class</b>InstanceOfExample {<b>public static void</b>main(String[] args) {Integer a =</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><b>new</b>Integer(5);<b>if </b>(a <b>instanceof </b>java.lang.Integer) { System.<i>out</i>.println(<b>true</b>);</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">} <b>else </b>{ System.<i>out</i>.println(<b>false</b>);</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Since a is integer object it returns true.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">There will be a compile time check whether reference expression is subtype of destination type. If it is not a subtype then compile time error will be shown as Incompatible types</p></li><li data-list-text="36)"><h2 style="padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">What does null mean in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">When a reference variable doesn’t point to any value it is assigned null. Example : Employee employee;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">In the above example employee object is not instantiate so it is pointed no where</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="37)"><h2 style="padding-left: 27pt;text-indent: -20pt;text-align: left;">Can we have multiple classes in single file ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Yes we can have multiple classes in single file but it people rarely do that and not recommended. We can have multiple classes in File but only one class can be made public. If we try to make two classes in File public we get following compilation error.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">“The public type must be defined in its own file”.</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="38)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">What all access modifiers are allowed for top class ?</h2></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">For top level class only two access modifiers are allowed. public and default. If a class is declared as public it is visible everywhere.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">If a class is declared default it is visible only in same package.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">If we try to give private and protected as access modifier to class we get the below compilation error.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Illegal Modifier for the class only public,abstract and final are permitted.</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">39 ) What are packages in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Package is a mechanism to group related classes ,interfaces and enums in to a single module. Package can be declared using the following statement :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Syntax : package &lt;package-name&gt;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;"><u>Coding Convention : </u>package name should be declared in small letters. package statement defines the namespace.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">The main use of package is</p><ol id="l14"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">To resolve naming conflicts</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">For visibility control : We can define classes and interfaces that are not accessible outside the class.</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><ol id="l15"><li data-list-text="40)"><h2 style="padding-left: 42pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: left;">Can we have more than one package statement in source file ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">We can’t have more than one package statement in source file. In any <span class="s4">java </span>program there can be atmost only 1 package statement. We will get compilation error if we have more than one package statement in source file.</p></li><li data-list-text="41)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -26pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Can we define package statement after import statement in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can’t define package statement after import statement in java. package statement must be the first statement in source file. We can have comments before the package statement.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="42)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">What are identifiers in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Identifiers are names in <span class="s4">java </span>program. Identifiers can be class name, method name or variable name. <u>Rules for defining identifiers in java:</u></p><ol id="l16"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Identifiers must start with letter,Underscore or dollar($) sign.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Identifiers can’t start with numbers .</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">There is no limit on number of characters in identifier but not recommended to have more than 15 characters</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Java identifiers are case sensitive.</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">First letter can be alphabet ,or underscore and dollar sign. From second letter we can have numbers</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">.</p></li><li data-list-text="6)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">We should’nt use reserve words for identifiers in java.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="43)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">What are access modifiers in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">The important feature of encapsulation is access control. By preventing access control we can misuse of class, methods and members.</p><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">A class, method or variable can be accessed is determined by the access modifier. There are three types of access modifiers in java. public,private,protected. If no access modifier is specified then it has a default access.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="44)"><h2 style="padding-left: 30pt;text-indent: -23pt;text-align: left;">What is the difference between access specifiers and access modifiers in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">In C++ we have access specifiers as public,private,protected and default and access modifiers as static, final. But there is no such divison of access specifiers and access modifiers in java. In Java we have access modifiers and non access modifiers.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Access Modifiers : public, private, protected, default Non Access Modifiers : abstract, final, stricfp.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="45)"><h2 style="padding-left: 55pt;text-indent: -48pt;text-align: left;">What access modifiers can be used for class ?</h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">We can use only two access modifiers for class public and default. <span class="s15">public:</span> A class with public modifier can be visible</p><ol id="l17"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package nonsubclass</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span class="s15">default :</span><span><table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0"><tr><td><img width="26" height="1" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAABoAAAABCAYAAADAW76WAAAABmJLR0QA/wD/AP+gvaeTAAAACXBIWXMAAA7EAAAOxAGVKw4bAAAAEElEQVQImWNkYGD4z0AHAABlbQEB6fGPvgAAAABJRU5ErkJgggAA"/></td></tr></table></span>A class with default modifier can be accesed</p><ol id="l18"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package nonsubclass</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the different package non subclass.</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="46)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">Explain what access modifiers can be used for methods?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can use all access modifiers public, private,protected and default for methods. <span class="s17">public</span><u> : </u>When a method is declared as public it can be accessed</p><ol id="l19"><li data-list-text="6)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="7)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="8)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package nonsubclass</p></li><li data-list-text="9)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="10)"><p style="padding-left: 31pt;text-indent: -24pt;text-align: left;">In the different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s18" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">default : <span style=" color: #000;">When a method is declared as default, we can access that method in</span></p><ol id="l20"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package non subclass</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We cannot access default access method in</p><ol id="l21"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span class="s17">protected : </span>When a method is declared as protected it can be accessed</p><ol id="l22"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">With in the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">With in the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">With in the same package non subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">With in different package subclass</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">It cannot be accessed non subclass in different package.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s18" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 3pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">private : <span style=" color: #000;">When a method is declared as private it can be accessed only in that class. It cannot be accessed in</span></p><ol id="l23"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Same package non subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="47)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -29pt;text-align: left;">Explain what access modifiers can be used for variables?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can use all access modifiers public, private,protected and default for variables. <span class="s17">public :&nbsp; </span>When a variables is declared as public it can be accessed</p><ol id="l24"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 86pt;text-indent: -79pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 86pt;text-indent: -79pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 86pt;text-indent: -79pt;text-align: left;">In the same package nonsubclass</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 86pt;text-indent: -79pt;text-align: left;">In the different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 86pt;text-indent: -79pt;text-align: left;">In the different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s18" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><u>default :</u> <span style=" color: #000;">When a variables is declared as default, we can access that method in</span></p><ol id="l25"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">In the same package non subclass</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We cannot access default access variables in</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package subclass</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">Different package non subclass.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s18" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><u>protected :</u> <span style=" color: #000;">When a variables is declared as protected it can be accessed</span></p><ol id="l26"><li data-list-text="1)"><p
