0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="124)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 40pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain purpose of sleep() method in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">sleep() method causes current running thread to sleep for specified amount of time . sleep() method is the minimum amount of the time the current thread sleeps but not the exact amount of time.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Signature :</p><p style="padding-left: 9pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public static native void sleep(long millis) throws InterruptedException</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public static void sleep(long millis, int nanos) throws InterruptedException {</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="125)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Assume a thread has lock on it, calling sleep() method on that thread will release the lock?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Calling sleep() method on thread which has lock does’nt affect. Lock will not be released though the thread sleeps for a specified amount of time.</p></li><li data-list-text="126)"><h2 style="padding-left: 43pt;text-indent: -36pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Can sleep() method causes another thread to sleep?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">No sleep() method causes current thread to sleep not any other thread.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="127)"><h2 style="padding-left: 46pt;text-indent: -36pt;text-align: justify;">Explain about interrupt() method of thread class ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">Thread class interrupt() method is used to interrupt current thread or another thread. It doesnot mean the current thread to stop immediately, it is polite way of telling or requesting to continue your present work. That is the reason we may not see the impact of interrupt call immediately.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Initially thread has a boolean property(interrupted status) false. So when we call interrupt() method status would set to true. This causes the current thread to continue its work and does not have impact immediately.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If a thread is in sleeping or waiting status (i.e thread has executed wait () or sleep() method) thread gets interrupted it stops what it is doing and throws an interrupted exception. This is reason we need to handle interrupted exception with throws or try/ catch block.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="128)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about interthread communication and how it takes place in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Usually threads are created to perform different unrelated tasks but there may be situations where they may perform related tasks. Interthread communication in <span class="s4">java </span>is done with the help of following three methods :</p><ol id="l52"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">wait()</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">notify()</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 29pt;text-indent: -22pt;text-align: left;">notifyAll()</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="129)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain wait(), notify() and notifyAll() methods of object class ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><u>wait() :</u> wait() method() makes the thread current thread sleeps and releases the lock until some other thread acquires the lock and calls notify().</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">notify() :notify() method wakes up the thread that called wait on the same object.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">notfiyAll() :notifyAll() method wakes up all the threads that are called wait() on the same object. The highest priority threads will run first.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">All the above three methods are in object class and are called only in synchronized context.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">All the above three methods must handle InterruptedException by using throws clause or by using try catch clause.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="130)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Explain why wait() , notify() and notifyAll() methods are in Object class rather than in thread class?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">First to know why they are in object class we should know what wait(), notify(), notifyAll() methods do. wait() , notify(), notifyAll() methods are object level methods they are called on same object.wait(), notify(), notifyAll() are called on an shared object so to they are kept in object class rather than thread class.</p></li><li data-list-text="131)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Explain IllegalMonitorStateException and when it will be thrown? <span class="p">IllegalMonitorStateException is thrown when wait(), notify() and notifyAll() are called in non synchronized context. Wait(), notify(),notifyAll() must always be called in synchronized context other wise we get this run time exception.</span></h2></li><li data-list-text="132)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">when wait(), notify(), notifyAll() methods are called does it releases the lock or holds the acquired lock?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">wait(), notify(), notifyAll() methods are always called in synchronized context. When these methods are called in synchronized context.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">So when they enter first in synchronized context thread acquires the lock on current object. When wait(), notify(), notifyAll() methods are called lock is released on that object.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="133)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Explain which of the following methods releases the lock when yield(), join(),sleep(),wait(),notify(), notifyAll() methods are executed?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Releases lock (Yes or No)</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">yield()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">No</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">sleep()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">No</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">join()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">No</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">wait()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Yes</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Notify()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Yes</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:114pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">notifyAll()</p></td><td style="width:215pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Yes</p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="134)"><h2 style="padding-left: 40pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What are thread groups?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Thread Groups are group of threads and other thread groups. It is a way of grouping threads so that actions can be performed on set of threads for easy maintenance and security purposes.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">For example we can start and stop all thread groups. We rarely use thread group class. By default all the threads that are created belong to default thread group of the main thread. Every thread belongs to a thread group. Threads that belong to a particular thread group cannot modify threads belonging to another thread group.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="135)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What are thread local variables ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Thread local variables are variables associated to a particular thread rather than object. We declare ThreadLocal object as private static variable in a class. Everytime a new thread accesses object by using getter or setter we are accesing copy of object. Whenever a thread calls get or set method of ThreadLocal instance a new copy is associated with particular object.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="136)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What are daemon threads in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Daemon threads are threads which run in background. These are service threads and works for the benefit of other threads. Garbage collector is one of the good example for daemon threads.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">By default all threads are non daemon. Daemon nature of a thread can be inherited. If parent thread is daemon , child thread also inherits daemon nature of thread.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="137)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">How to make a non daemon thread as daemon?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">By default all threads are non daemon. We can make non daemon nature of thread to daemon by using setDaemon() method. The important point to note here we can call setDaemon() only before start() method is called on it. If we call setDaemon() after start() method an IllegalThreadStateException will be thrown.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="138)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can we make main() thread as daemon?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Main thread is always non daemon. We cannot change the non daemon nature of main thread to daemon.</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Interview questions on Nested classses and inner classes</p></li><li data-list-text="139)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What are nested classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Class declared with in another class is defined as nested class. There are two types of nested classes in java.</p><ol id="l53"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Static nested class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Non static nested class</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A static nested class has static keyword declared before class definition.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="140)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What are inner classes or non static nested classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Nested classes without any static keyword declaration in class definition are defined as non static nested classes. Generally non static nested classes are referred as inner classes.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">There are three types of inner classes in java :</p><ol id="l54"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Local inner class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Member inner class</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Anonymous inner class</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="141)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Why to use nested classes in java? (or)</h2><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">What is the purpose of nested class in java?</h2><ol id="l55"><li data-list-text="1)"><p class="s15" style="padding-left: 16pt;text-indent: -9pt;text-align: left;"> Grouping of related classes</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Classes which are not reusable can be defined as inner class instead of creating inner class.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">For example : We have a submit button upon click of submit button we need to execute some code. This code is related only to that class and cannot be reused for other class . Instead of creating a new class we can create inner class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p class="s16" style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">To increase encapsulation :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Inner class can access private members of outer class.so by creating getter and setter methods for private variables , outside world can access these variables. But by creating inner class private variables can be accesed only by inner class.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p class="s16" style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Code readable and maintainable :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Rather than creating a new class we can create inner class so that it is easy to maintain.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p class="s16" style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Hiding implementation :</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Inner class helps us to hide implementation of class.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="142)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about static nested classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When a static class is defined inside a enclosing class we define that as nested class. Static nested classes are not inner classes. Static nested classes can be instantiated without instance of outer class.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A static nested doesnot have access to instance variables and non static methods of outer class.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="143)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">How to instantiate static nested classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">We can access static members and static methods of outer class without creating any instance of outer class.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Syntax for instantiating Static nested class :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">OuterclassName.StaticNestedClassName ref=new OuterclassName.StaticNestedClassName();</p></li><li data-list-text="144)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about method local inner classes or local inner classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Nested classes defined inside a method are local inner classes. We can create objects of local inner class only inside method where class is defined. A local inner classes exist only when method is invoked and goes out of scope when method returns.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="145)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about features of local inner class?</h2><ol id="l56"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">Local inner class does not have any access specifier.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We cannot use access modifiers static for local inner class. But we can use abstract and final for local inner class.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">We cannot declare static members inside local inner classes.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">We can create objects of local inner class only inside method where class is defined.</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">Method local inner classes can only access final variables declared inside a method.</p></li><li data-list-text="6)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">Method local inner classes can be defined inside loops(for,while) and blocks such as if etc.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="146)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about anonymous inner classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Inner class defined without any class name is called anonymous inner class. Inner class is declared and instantiated using new keyword.The main purpose of anonymous inner classes in <span class="s4">java </span>are to provide interface implementation. We use anonymous classes when we need only one instance for a class. We can use all members of enclosing class and final local variables.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When we compile anonymous inner classes compiler creates two files</p><ol id="l57"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">EnclosingName.class</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">EnclsoingName$1.class</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="147)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain restrictions for using anonymous inner classes?</h2><ol id="l58"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">An anonymous inner class cannot have any constructor because there is no name for class.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">An anonymous inner class cannot define static methods, fields or classes.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">We cannot define an interface anonymously.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">Anonymous inner class can be instantiated only once.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="148)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Is this valid in java ? can we instantiate interface in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Runnable r = new Runnable() { @Override</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">public void run() {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">};</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Runnable is an interface.If we see the above code it looks like we are instantiating Runnable interface. But we are not instantiating interface we are instantiating anonymous inner class which is implementation of Runnable interface.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="149)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about member inner classes?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Non static class defined with in enclosing class are called member inner class. A member inner class is defined at member level of class. A member inner class can access the members of outer class including private members.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Features of member inner classes :</p><ol id="l59"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">A member inner class can be declared abstract or final.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">A member inner class can extend class or implement interface.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">An inner class cannot declare static fields or methods.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">A member inner class can be declared with public, private, protected or default access.</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="150)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">How to instantiate member inner class?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">OuterClassName.InnerclassName inner=new OuterClassReference.new InnerClassName(); We cannot instantiate inner class without outer class reference</p></li><li data-list-text="151)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">How to do encapsulation in Java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Make instance variables private.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Define getter and setter methods to access instance variables .</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="152)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What are reference variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Variables which are used to access objects in <span class="s4">java </span>are called reference variables. Ex : Employee emp=new Employee();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In the above example emp is reference variable. Reference variable can be of only one type.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A reference variable can point to any number of objects. But if a reference variable is declared final it can’t point to other objects.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A reference variable can be declared either to a class type or interface type. If a reference variable is declared with interface type it points to the class that implements the interface.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="153)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Will the compiler creates a default constructor if I have a parameterized constructor in the class?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">No compiler won’t create default constructor if there is parameterized constructor in the class. For example if I have a class with no constructors, then compiler will create default constructor.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For Example :</p><p class="s12" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public class<span class="p">Car {}</span></p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In the above Car class there are no constructors so compiler creates a default constructor.</p><p class="s12" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public class<span class="p">Car {Car(String name) {</span></p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In this example compiler won’t create any default constructor because already there is one constructor in the Car class.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="154)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Can we have a method name same as class name in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Yes we can have method name same as class name it won’t throw any compilation error but it shows a warning message that method name is same as class name.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="155)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Can we override constructors in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Only methods can be overridden in java. Constructors can’t be inherited in java. So there is no point of verriding constructors in java.</p></li><li data-list-text="156)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can Static methods access instance variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">No.Instance variables can’t be accessed in static methods. When we try to access instance variable in static method we get compilation error. The error is as follows:</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Cannot make a static reference to the non static field name</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="157)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">How do we access static members in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Instance variables and instance methods can be accessed using reference variable . But to access static variables or static methods we use Class name in java.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="158)"><h2 style="padding-left: 40pt;text-indent: -33pt;text-align: left;">Can we override static methods in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Static methods can’t be overridden. If we have a static method in superclass and subclass with same signature then we don’t say that as overriding. We call that as</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="159)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between object and reference?</h2></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Reference and object are both different. Objects are instances of class that resides in heap memory. Objects does’nt have any name so to access objects we use references. There is no alternative way to access objects except through references.</p><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Object cannot be assigned to other object and object cannot be passed as an argument to a method. Reference is a variable which is used to access contents of an object. A reference can be assigned to other reference ,passed to a method.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">160 ) Objects or references which of them gets garbage collected?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Objects get garbage collected not its references.</p><ol id="l60"><li data-list-text="161)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">How many times finalize method will be invoked ? who invokes finalize() method in java? <span class="p">Finalize () method will be called only once on object. Before the object gets garbage collected garbage collector will call finalize() method to free the resources. Finalize() method will be called only when object is eligible for garbage collection.</span></h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="162)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can we able to pass objects as an arguments in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Only references can be passed to a method not an object. We cannot pass the objects to a method. The largest amount of data that can passed as parameters are long or double.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="163)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain wrapper classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Converting primitives to objects can be done with the help of wrapper classes. Prior to <span class="s4">java </span>1.5 we use Wrapper classes to convert primitives to objects. From java 1.5 we have a new feature autoboxing which is used to convert automatically primitives to objects but in wrapper classes programmer has to take care of converting primitives to objects.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Wrapper classes are immutable in java. Once a value is assigned to it we cannot change the value.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="164)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain different types of wrapper classes in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">For every primitive in java we have corresponding wrapper class. Here are list of wrapper classes available in java.</p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Primtive</p></td><td class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">boolean</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Boolean</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">int</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Integer</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">float</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Float</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p
