style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Character</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">byte</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Byte</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">long</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Long</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:122pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">short</p></td><td style="width:198pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Short</p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="165)"><h2 style="padding-left: 36pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about transient variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">To save the state of an object to persistent state we use serialization. If we want a field or variable in the object not to be saved, then we declare that variable or field as transient.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Example : public Class Car implements serializable</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">transient int carnumber;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p></li><li data-list-text="166)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can we serialize static variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Static variables cannot be serialized in java.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="167)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What is type conversion in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Assigning a value of one type to variable of other type is called type conversion. Example : int a =10;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">long b=a;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">There are two types of conversion in java:</p><ol id="l61"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Widening conversion</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Narrowing conversion</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="168)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about Automatic type conversion in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span class="s4">Java </span>automatic type conversion is done if the following conditions are met :</p><ol id="l62"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When two types are compatible Ex : int, float</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">int can be assigned directly to float variable.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Destination type is larger than source type. Ex : int, long</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: justify;">Int can be assigned directly to long .Automatic type conversion takes place if int is assigned to long because long is larger datatype than int.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Widening Conversion comes under Automatic type conversion.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="169)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: justify;">Explain about narrowing conversion in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">When destination type is smaller than source type we use narrowing conversion mechanism in java. Narrowing conversion has to be done manually if destination type is smaller than source type. To do narrowing conversion we use cast. Cast is nothing but explicit type conversion.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Example : long a; byte b; b=(byte)a;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Note : casting to be done only on valid types otherwise classcastexception will be thrown.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="170)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain the importance of import keyword in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Import keyword is used to import single class or package in to our source file.import statement is declared after package decalaration. We use wild character (*) to import package.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Note : After compilation the compiled code does not contain import statement it will be replaced with fully qualified class names</p></li><li data-list-text="171)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Explain naming conventions for packages ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Sun defined standard naming conventions for packages.</p><ol id="l63"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Package names should be in small letters.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Package name starts with reverse company domain name (excluding www) followed by department and project name and then the name of package.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Example : com.google.sales.employees</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="172)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is classpath ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">The path where our .class files are saved is referred as classpath.JVM searches for .class files by using the class path specified. Class path is specified by using CLASSPATH environment variable. CLASSPATH environment variable can contain more than one value. CLASSPATH variable containing more than one value is separated by semicolon.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Example to set class path from command prompt :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">set CLASSPATH= C:Program FilesJavajdk1.6.0_25bin;.;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">only parent directories need to be added to classpath.<span class="s4">Java </span>compiler will look for appropriate packages and classes.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="173)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is jar ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Jar stands for java archive file. Jars are created by using Jar.exe tool. Jar files contains .class files, other resources used in our application and manifest file.Manifest file contains class name with main method.jar contains compressed .class files. Jvm finds these .class files without uncompressing this jar.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="174)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is the scope or life time of instance variables ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When object is instantiated using new operator variables get allocated in the memory.instance variables remain in memory till the instance gets garbage collected</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="175)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain the scope or life time of class variables or static variables?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Static variables do not belong to instances of the class. We can access static fields even before instantiating the class. Static variable remain in memory till the life time of application.</p></li><li data-list-text="176)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Explain scope or life time of local variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Local variables are variables which are defined inside a method. When the method is created local variables gets created in stack memory and this variable gets deleted from memory once the method execution is done.</p></li><li data-list-text="177)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about static imports in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">From <span class="s4">Java </span>5.0 we can import static variables in to source file. Importing static member to source file is referred as static import. The advantage of static import is we can access static variables without class or interface name.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Syntax : import static packagename.classname.staticvariablename; Ex : import static com.abc.Employee.eno;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">To import all static variables from a class in to our source file we use *. import static com.abc.Employee.*</p></li><li data-list-text="178)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can we define static methods inside interface?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">We can’t declare static methods inside interface. Only instance methods are permitted in interfaces.only public and abstract modifiers are permitted for interface methods. If we try to declare static methods inside interface we get compilation error saying</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">“Illegal modifier for the interface method Classname.methodName(); only public &amp; abstract are permitted”.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="179)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Define interface in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Interface is collection of abstract methods and constants. An interface is also defined as pure or 100 percent abstract class.Interfaces are implicitly abstract whether we define abstract access modifier or not. A class implementing interface overrides all the abstract methods defined in interface. Implements keyword is used to implement interface.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="180)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is the purpose of interface?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Interface is a contract . Interface acts like a communication between two objects. When we are defining interface we are defining a contract what our class should do but not how it does. An interface does’nt define what a method does. The power of interface lies when different classes that are unrelated can implement interface. Interfaces are designed to support dynamic method resolution at run time.</p></li><li data-list-text="181)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain features of interfaces in java?</h2><ol id="l64"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">All the methods defined in interfaces are implicitly abstract even though abstract modifier is not declared.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">All the methods in interface are public whether they are declared as public or not.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">variables declared inside interface are by default public, static and final.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Interfaces cannot be instantiated.</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">we cannot declare static methods inside interface.</p></li><li data-list-text="6)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">‘ implements’ keyword is used to implement interface.</p></li><li data-list-text="7)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Unlike class, interface can extend any number of interfaces.</p></li><li data-list-text="8)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">We can define a class inside interface and the class acts like inner class to interface.</p></li><li data-list-text="9)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">An interface can extend a class and implement an interface</p></li><li data-list-text="10)"><p style="padding-left: 28pt;text-indent: -21pt;text-align: left;">Multiple inheritance in <span class="s4">java </span>is achieved through interfaces.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="182)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: justify;">Explain enumeration in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">Enumeration is a new feature from Java 5.0. Enumeration is set of named constants . We use enum keyword to declare enumeration. The values defined in enumeration are enum constants.Each enum constant declared inside a enum class is by default public , static and final.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: justify;">Example :</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">package <span class="p">javaexamples;</span></p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: justify;">public enum <span class="p">Days {</span></p><p class="s20" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">SUN<span class="p">,</span>MON<span class="p">,</span>TUE<span class="p">,</span>WED<span class="p">,</span>THU<span class="p">,</span>FRI<span class="p">,</span>SAT;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p class="s20" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">SUN<span class="p">,</span>MON<span class="p">,</span>TUE<span class="p">,</span>WED<span class="p">,</span>THU<span class="p">,</span>FRI<span class="p">,</span>SAT are enum constants.</p></li><li data-list-text="183)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain restrictions on using enum?</h2><ol id="l65"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">Enums cannot extend any other class or enum.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">We cannot instantiate an enum.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can declare fields and methods in enum class. But these fields and methods should follow the enum constants otherwise we get compilation error.</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="184)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about field hiding in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If superclass and subclass have same fields subclass cannot override superclass fields. In this case subclass fields hides the super class fields. If we want to use super class variables in subclass we use super keyword to access super class variables.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="185)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about Varargs in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Beginning with <span class="s4">Java </span>5 has a new feature Varargs which allows methods to have variable number of arguments. It simplifies creation of methods when there are more number of arguments. Earlier to java 5 Varargs are handled by creating method with array of arguments.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex : public static void main(String[] args)</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">A variable length argument is specified using ellispses with type in signature. main method with var args is written as follows:</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">public static void main(String … args)</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">If no arguments are passes we get array with size 0.There is no need for null check if no arguments are passed.</p></li><li data-list-text="186)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: justify;">Explain where variables are created in memory?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">When we declare variables variables are created in stack. So when the variable is out of scope those variables get garbage collected.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="187)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: justify;">Can we use Switch statement with Strings?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: justify;">Prior to Java 7 we can use only int values and enum constants in Switch .Starting with Java 7 we can use strings in Switch statement. If we use strings in switch statement prior to Java 7 we will get compile time error “only int and enum constants are permitted”.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="188)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">In java how do we copy objects?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In Java we cannot copy two objects but by assigning one reference to other we can copy objects. For example if we have a reference r1 that point to object .so when we declare r2=r1, we are assigning reference r1 to r2 so now r2 points to the same object where r1 points. Any changes done by one reference on an object will reflect to other.</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Oops concepts interview questions</p></li><li data-list-text="189)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Explain about procedural programming language or structured programming language and its features?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In traditional programming language to solve a problem we use set of procedures. Once the procedures or functions are determined next they concentrate on storing data.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Features :</p><ol id="l66"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In this top down approach is followed. First procedures were determined and then concentrate on minute details.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Concentrate more on functions and procedure rather than data.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In traditional programming language procedures manipulate global data without knowing to other procedures.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Very little concentration on minute details</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The main drawback of traditional programming languages works well only for small problems. But not suitable for larger problems.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex : C language, Pascal</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="190)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about object oriented programming and its features?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span class="s4">Java </span>replaced traditional programming language developed in 1970’s. In Object oriented programming everything is made up of object. In this language bottom up approach is followed. Each</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">object communicates with other as opposed to traditional view. <u>Features :</u></p><ol id="l67"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In this bottom approach is followed. First concentrates on minute details like creating objects then concentrates on implementation or solving the problem.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Concentrate more on data and give less importance for implementation.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Objects communicate with each other</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The main advantage of object oriented programming language is works well for larger problems.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="191)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">List out benefits of object oriented programming language?</h2><ol id="l68"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Easy maintenance</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Code reusability</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Code extendability</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Reliable</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="192)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Differences between traditional programming language and object oriented programming language?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Traditional Programming language</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Object Oriented Programming Language</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A program is divided in to modules and procedures.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A program is divided in to number of objects.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Implementation is done through procedures.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Implementation is done through interfaces.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">In traditional programming there is no encapsulation all procedures access data.</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">In oops encapsulation is done by tightly coupling data and behaviour together in class.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Suitable for small programs or problems</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Suitable for large programs and complex problems.</p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="193)"><h2 style="padding-left: 40pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain oops concepts in detail?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Object oriented programming should support these three features :</p><ol id="l69"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Inheritance</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Encapsulation</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Polymorphism</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="194)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain what is encapsulation?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Encapsulation is the process of wrapping of code and behaviour in a single unit called class and preventing from misuse is called encapsulation. Encapsulation exposes only part of object which are safe to exposed and remaining part of object is kept secured.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Encapsulation is supported through access control in java. There are four types of access control specifiers(public,private, protected, default) in <span class="s4">java </span>which supports encapsulation.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">For example tv manufacturers exposes only buttons not all the thousands of electronic components which it is made up of.</p></li><li data-list-text="195)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">What is inheritance ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Inheritance is one of the important feature of object oriented language. Inheriting is the process of acquiring features of others. For example a child acquires the features of their parents.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">In java inheritance is the process of inheriting member of existing classes by extending their functionality. The original class is called base class, parent class or super class. The new class derived from parent is called child class, sub class, and derived class.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We use extends keyword in java to extend a class in java. All java classes extend java.lang.Object since object class is the super class for all classes in java.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When we create a new class by using inheritance ‘is-a’ relationship is formed.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="196)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain importance of inheritance in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Reusability :The major advantage of inheritance is code reuse. We can avoid duplicating code by using inheritance. We can place all common state and behaviour in that class , by extending that class we can Extendability : We can add new functionality to our application without touching the existing code.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">For example if we take Ms word we came across number of versions of msword such as word 2003,2007. Everytime they won’t write new code they reuse the existing code and some more features.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="197)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is polymorphism in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Polymorphism is combination of two greek words which mean many forms. In polymorphism actual type of object involved in method call determines which method to call rather type of reference variable.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">59) What is covariant return ?</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">In java 1.4 and earlier one method can override super class method if both methods have same signature and return types.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">From Java 1.5 , a method can override other method if argument types match exactly though return types are different.(Return type must be subtype of other method).</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Example : Class A</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A doSomeThing()</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">return new A();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Example : Class B</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">B doSomeThing()</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">return new B();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">From java 1.5 return type for doSomeThing() in Class B is valid . We get compile time error in 1.4 and earlier.</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Collection Framework interview questions</p></li><li data-list-text="198)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is collections framework ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">A framework is set of classes and interfaces to build a functionality. <span class="s4">Java </span>collections framework provides set of interfaces and classes for storing and manipulating collections. Collection framework contains classes and interfaces in java.util package and java.util.concurrent packages.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Advantages or benefits of Collections framework :</p><ol id="l70"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">High performance</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Using this framework we can create different types of collections</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">We can create our own collection and we can extend a collection.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Reduces programming effort.</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Increases speed and quality : Collections framework provides high performance, implementations of useful data structures and algorithms.</p></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="199)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is collection ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">A collection is a container which holds group of objects. Collection provides a way to manage objects easily. Collections manages group of objects as single unit.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Examples include list of strings, integers etc.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Here are few basic operations we do on collections :</p><ol id="l71"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Adding objects to collection.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Removing or deleting objects from collection.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Retrieving object from collection.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Iterating collection.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="200)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between collection, Collection and Collections in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">collection : represent group of objects where objects are stored.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Collection : This is one of the core interface which provides basic functionality for collection. Collections : Collections contains some utility static methods that operate on collections.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="201)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about Collection interface in java ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Collection is the fundamental and root interface in Collections framework. Collection extends Iterable interface and inherits iterator method which returns Iterator object.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Signature :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public interface Collection&lt;E&gt; extends Iterable&lt;E&gt; {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Methods in Collection interface :</p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">boolean add(E e);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Adds an element to the collection. Returns true if element is added.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">boolean remove(Object o);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Removes an object from collection if that object is present in collection. Return true if matching object is removed from collection.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 9pt;text-align: left;">boolean addAll(Collection&lt;?</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">extends E&gt; c);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Adds all the elements specified in the collection to this collection.Returns true if all elements are added.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">boolean removeAll(Collection&lt;?&gt;</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">c);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Removes all the elements from this collection that are specified in other collection.Returns true if all the elements are removed.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">int size();</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Returns number of elements in collection.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">boolean isEmpty();</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Checks whether collection contains elements or not. If no elements are present it returns false.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">boolean contains(Object o);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Checks whether specified object is in collection or not. Return true if object is in collection.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Iterator&lt;E&gt; iterator();</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Used to iterator over collection. No guarantee on order of elements iterated.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">boolean</p><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 3pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">retainAll(Collection&lt;?&gt; c);</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Removes all the elements which are not in specified collection. Returns only elements specified in collection removing other elements.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:118pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Object[] toArray();</p></td><td style="width:361pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns an array of elements in collection.</p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="202)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">List the interfaces which extends collection interface ?</h2><ol id="l72"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">List</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Set</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Queue</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Deque ( From Java 6)</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="203)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain List interface ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">List interface extends collection interface used to store sequence of elements in collection. We can even store duplicate elements in list.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">We can insert or access elements in list by using index as we do in arrays. List is an ordered collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">The main difference between List and non list interface are methods based on position.</p><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Some of the operations we can perform on List :</p><ol id="l73"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Adding an element at specified index.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Removing an element at specified index.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">To get the index of element</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">List contains some specific methods apart from Collection interface methods.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="204)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain methods specific to List interface ?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method returns an element at specified position in the list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">E set(int index, E element);</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method replaces the element at specified position in the list with the specified element.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">void add(int index, E element);</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method inserts the specified element with the index specified.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">E remove(int index);</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method removes the element at specified index and returns the element removed.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">int indexOf(Object o);</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">indexOf() method returns the index of last occurrence of specified element. If there is no</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">element in the list it removes the element.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">ListIterator&lt;E&gt; listIterator();</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns a list iterator of elements in list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:240pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">List&lt;E&gt; subList(int fromIndex, int toIndex);</p></td><td style="width:239pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 7pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method returns list of elements between indexes specified.</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="205)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">List implementations of List Interface ?</h2><ol id="l74"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">ArrayList</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Vector</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">LinkedList</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="206)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain about ArrayList ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">ArrayList is an ordered collection which extends AbstractList and implements List interface. We use ArrayList mainly when we need faster access and fast iteration of elements in list. We can insert nulls in to arraylist.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Arraylist is nothing but a growable array.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s12" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">public class ArrayList&lt;E&gt; extends AbstractList&lt;E&gt; implements List&lt;E&gt;, RandomAccess, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable{}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">From <span class="s4">java </span>1.4 ArrayList implements RandomAccess interface which is a marker interface which supports fast and random access.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Advantages :</p><ol id="l75"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Faster and easier access.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Used for Random access of elements. <u>Drawbacks :</u></p><ol id="l76"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">We cannot insert or delete elements from middle of list.</p></li></ol></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="207)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between Array and ArrayList ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Arrays are used to store primitives or objects of same type or variables that are subclasses of same type. ArrayList : It is an ordered collection which grows dynamically.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">In list we can insert nulls values and list allows duplicate elements.</p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s24" style="padding-right: 12pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: center;">ARRAY</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s24" style="padding-left: 68pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">ARRAY LIST</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">1)  While creating array we have to know the size.</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 4pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">1)  But it is not required to know size while creating ArrayList, because arraylist grows dynamically.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:45pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">2) To put an element in to array we use the following syntax :String array[] = <b>new</b>String[5];array[1] = “java”;We must know</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">specific location to insert an element in to</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">2) We can add element to arraylist with following syntax :List&lt;String&gt; stringList = new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;();stringList.add(“java”);</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">array. If we try to put element in index which is out of range we get ArrayIndexOutOfBounds Exception</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">3) Arrays are static</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">3) ArrayList is dynamic</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">4) We can store objects and primitives</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">4) We can store only primitives prior to 1.5 . From</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">1.5 we can store even objects also.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5) We have to manually write logic for inserting and removing elements.</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 4pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">5) Just a method call would add or remove elements from list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">6) Arrays are faster</p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">6) Arraylist is slower.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:222pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td><td style="width:238pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">7) Arraylist is implemented using arrays.</p></td></tr></table></li><li data-list-text="208)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What is vector?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Vector is similar to arraylist used for random access. Vector is a dynamic array like arraylist.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">vector size increases or decreases when elements are added and removed . Vector is synchronized .</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">vector and Hashtable are the only collections since 1.0. Rest of the collections are added from 2.0.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">public class Vector&lt;E&gt;extends AbstractList&lt;E&gt;implements List&lt;E&gt;, RandomAccess, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/></li><li data-list-text="209)"><h2 style="padding-top: 9pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between arraylist and vector ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Both ArrayList and vector grows dynamically. The differences between arraylist and vector are :</p><ol id="l77"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Arraylist is not synchronized and vector is synchronized.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Vector is legacy collection introduced in 1.0 and Arraylist introduced in <span class="s4">java </span>2.0.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Performance wise it is recommended to use arraylist rather than vector because by default vector is synchronized which reduces performance if only one thread accesses it.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="210)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Define Linked List and its features with signature ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Linked list is used for storing a collection of objects that allows efficient addition and removal of elements in the middle of the collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">The main drawback with arrays is if we want to insert an element in the middle of the list we need to move each element to next position and insert the element. Similarly with remove if we want to remove an element we need to remove the element and move the list of elements.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">But with linked list we can insert and delete in the middle of the list efficiently by just updating the neighbouring node reference.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Linked list class is in java.util package.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Linked List class extends class extends AbstractSequentialList and I mplements List, Deque, Cloneable and Serializable.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-top: 2pt;padding-left: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Signature :<b>public class LinkedList&lt;E&gt; extends AbstractSequentialList&lt;E&gt;</b></p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 13pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">implements List&lt;E&gt;, Deque&lt;E&gt;, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Important methods specific to LinkedList class :</p><ol id="l78"><li data-list-text="1)"><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;"> public E getFirst() :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><u>getFirst() will </u>returns the first element in the list.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">public E getLast() :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">getLast() returns the last element in the list.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">public E removeFirst() :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">removeFirst() method removes the first element in the list.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">public E removeLast() :</p><p style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">removeLast() method removes the last element in the list.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 41pt;text-indent: -35pt;text-align: left;">public void addFirst(E e)</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Inserts the element at beginning of the list.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="6)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">public void addLast(E e) :</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Inserts the element at end of the list.</p></li><li data-list-text="211)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Define Iterator and methods in Iterator?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If we want to iterate through all the elements in collection we use Iterator. Iterator is a standard way to access elements one by one in collection. Iterator is an object associated with collection used to loop through the collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Steps for accessing elements in Iterator :</p><ol id="l79"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Obtain Iterator object by calling iterator() method on collection. Ex : ArrayList &lt;String&gt; al=new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Iterator itr=al.iterator();</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Call hasNext() method on iterator object in loop as long as hasNext() returns true. Ex : while(itr.hasNext())</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Get each element by calling next() inside the loop. while(itr.hasNext())</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">String str=itr.next();</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p class="s16" style="padding-bottom: 1pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Methods in iterator :</p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:109pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method</p></td><td style="width:370pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Description</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:109pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">boolean hasNext();</p></td><td
