style="width:370pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">This method returns true if there is next element.hasNext() points to position before first lement.If there are any elements if will return true.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:109pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">E next();</p></td><td style="width:370pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns the next element in the iteration. . If there are no elements in the</p><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 2pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Iteration NoSuchElementException is thrown. next() will move the pointer to next position and returns the element.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:109pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">void remove();</p></td><td style="width:370pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Removes the element.</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: justify;">Note : If we call next() on last element it will throw java.util.NoSuchElementException. So before calling next() first we should call hasNext() whether it has elements or not. If there is next element we can call next() so that we can avoid exception.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="212)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">In which order the Iterator iterates over collection?</h2></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The order in which Iterator will iterate the collection depends on the traversal order of collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For example : for list traversal order will be sequential, and for set the order cannot be determined, and for sorted sorted set will sort the elements in sorted order.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">So it all depends on the collection in which order iterator iterates.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><ol id="l80"><li data-list-text="212)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain ListIterator and methods in ListIterator?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">List Iterator is similar to Iterator but ListIterator is bidirectional.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can traverse through the collection in either forward or backward direction.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">List Iterator extends Iterator and all the methods in Iterator will be there in ListIterator too with some additional methods .</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">List Iterator doesn’t have current element .Position of List Iterator lies between two elements i.e previous element and next element.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Features of ListIterator :</p><ol id="l81"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Traversal of List in either direction.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Modification of its elements.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Access to elements position.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Signature :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public interface ListIterator&lt;E&gt; extends Iterator&lt;E&gt; {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">ListIterator methods :</p><div class="textbox" style="border:0.7pt solid #A3A3A3;display:block;left:0.4pt;min-height:12.5pt;top:96.1pt;width:383.1pt;"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><span style=" color: black; font-family:Verdana, sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; text-decoration: underline; font-size: 8.5pt;">Description</span></p></div></li></ol><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Method</p><p style="padding-left: 5pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"/><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Void add(E obj)</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Inserts element in to the list infront of the element returned by call to next() and after the element returned by call to next().</p></td></tr><tr style="height:10pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 9pt;text-align: left;">boolean hasNext();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" rowspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Returns true if there are more elements in the list instead of throwing exception if there are no elements.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:88pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td><td style="width:7pt;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">E next();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Returns the next element . NoSuchElementException is thrown if there is no next element.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:10pt"><td style="width:7pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td><td style="width:88pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 9pt;text-align: left;">boolean</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" rowspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns true if there are elements when iterating list in reverse direction.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">hasPrevious();</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">E previous();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns the previous element in the list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">int nextIndex();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Returns the index of the element returned by next() method. If there are no elements it returns the size of the list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 3pt;text-indent: 6pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">int previousIndex();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Returns the index of the element returned by previous() method. If there are no</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">elements it returns the size of the list. Returns -1 if the iterator is at beginning of list.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">void remove();</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Removes the element that was returned by calling next() or previous(). An Illegal state Exception will be thrown if remove() is called before next() or previous().</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:95pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3" colspan="2"><p class="s6" style="padding-left: 13pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">void set(E e);</p></td><td style="width:384pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">This method replaces an element in the list with the specified element.</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><ol id="l82"><li data-list-text="213)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about Sets ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">A set is a collection which does not allow duplicates. Set internally implements equals() method which doesn’t allow duplicates.Adding an duplicate element to a set would be ignored .Set interface is implemented in java.util.set package.Set interface does not have any additional methods . It has only collection methods. A set can contain atmost one null value.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">ArrayList is an ordered collection.In arraylists order remains same in which they are inserted. But coming to set it is an unordered collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public interface Set&lt;E&gt; extends Collection&lt;E&gt; {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Important operations that can be performed on set :</p><ol id="l83"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Adding an element to set.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Removing an element from set.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Check if an element exist in set.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Iterating through set.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="214)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Implementations of Set interface ?</h2><ol id="l84"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">HashSet</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">Linked HashSet</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">TreeSet</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="215)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">Explain HashSet and its features ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Hashset implements set interface and extends AbstractSet. Features of Hashset are :</p><ol id="l85"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">It does not allow duplicates.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">It does not gurantee ordering of elements.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">It is unsorted and unordered set.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Performance wise it is recommended to use hashset when compared to other sets because it internally uses hashing mechanism.</p></li><li data-list-text="5)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Allows insertion of nulls.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Note : For efficiency whenever objects are added to HashSet it need to implement the hashCode() method.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">public class HashSet&lt;E&gt; extends AbstractSet&lt;E&gt; implements Set&lt;E&gt;, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p></li><li data-list-text="216)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain Tree Set and its features?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">TreeSet implements navigableSet interface and extends Abstract set.It creates collection that uses tree for storage.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Features of Treeset are :</p><ol id="l86"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">It does not allow duplicates.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 23pt;text-indent: -16pt;text-align: left;">When we retrieve the elements in treeset we will get elements in sorted order.</p></li></ol><p class="s12" style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public class <span class="p">TreeSet&lt;E&gt; </span>extends <span class="p">AbstractSet&lt;E&gt;</span></p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">implements <span class="p">NavigableSet&lt;E&gt;, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable</span></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p></li><li data-list-text="217)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">When do we use HashSet over TreeSet?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">If we want to search for an element in collection and does not want any sorting order we go for HashSet.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">82) When do we use TreeSet over HashSet? TreeSet is preferred</p><ol id="l87"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">if elements are to be maintained in sorting order.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Fast insertion and retrieval of elements.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="218)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">What is Linked HashSet and its features? <span class="p">LinkedHashSet extends HashSet and implements Set interface. public class LinkedHashSet&lt;E&gt;</span></h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">extends HashSet&lt;E&gt;</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">implements Set&lt;E&gt;, Cloneable, java.io.Serializable {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Linked HashSet is similar to HashSet but in linked HashSet we maintain order but in HashSet we don’t maintain order. Maintaining order means elements will be retrieved in order which they are inserted.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="219)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about Map interface in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">A map is an association of key-value pairs. Both keys and values in map are objects. <u>Features of map :</u></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">1)  Maps cannot have duplicate keys but can have duplicate value objects.</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="220)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is linked hashmap and its features?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">LinkedHashMap extends HashMap and implements Map.lLinked hashmap gurantees order of elements . Elements are retrieved in same order they are inserted.Linked HashMap uses internally double linked lists to keep insertion order.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The differences between Hashmap and linked hashmap is</p><ol id="l88"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">LinkedHashMap maintains the insertion order while HashMap doesnot maintain order.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">HashMap if faster for insertion and deletion of elements when compared to linked hashmap. Linked hashmap is preferred only for faster iteration of elements.</p></li></ol><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">public class <span class="p">LinkedHashMap&lt;K,V&gt; </span>extends <span class="p">HashMap&lt;K,V&gt; </span>implements <span class="p">Map&lt;K,V&gt;</span></p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">{</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p></li><li data-list-text="221)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What is SortedMap interface?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">SortedMap extends Map interface.Sorted Map <span class="s26">maintains sorted order of keys </span>in a map.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">By default sorted map <span class="s26">maintains natural ordering </span>if we want custom order we can specify using comparator.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">public interface SortedMap&lt;K,V&gt; extends Map&lt;K,V&gt; {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="222)"><h2 style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: -30pt;text-align: left;">What is Hashtable and explain features of Hashtable?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Hashtable was available before collection framework.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">When collection framework was started Hashtable extends Dictionary class and Map interface. Hashtable offers a convenient way of <span class="s26">storing key/ value pairs</span>.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Hashtable <span class="s26">does not allow nulls either keys or values</span>. Hashtable is <span class="s26">synchronized</span>.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="223)"><h2 style="padding-bottom: 1pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between HashMap and Hashtable?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Difference</p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 16pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">HashMap</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 22pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Hashtable</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Synronization</p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">HashMap is <span class="s27">not synchronized</span>.</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Hashtable is <span class="s27">synchronized</span>.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Nulls</p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">HashMap allows atmost <span class="s28">one null key and any number of null values</span>.</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Hashtable <span class="s28">does not allow null values</span>.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:23pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Performance</p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Since HashMap is not synchronized its performance is <span class="s28">faster than </span>Hashtable.</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Performance is <span class="s27">slower </span>when compared to HashMap.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Introduction</p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">HashMap introduced starting from</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Hashtable is even before collection</p></td></tr></table><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:104pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></td><td style="width:180pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">collection framework.</p></td><td style="width:195pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">framework.</p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="224)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between arraylist and linkedlist?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:127pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 16pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Difference</p></td><td style="width:189pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 37pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Arraylist</p></td><td style="width:163pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 25pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">LinkedList</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:127pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Access</p></td><td style="width:189pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Implements RandomAccess interface we can <span class="s28">search randomly </span>all the elements</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">in the list.</p></td><td style="width:163pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">It extends Abstract sequential List interface which provides</p><p class="s28" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">sequential access <span class="s6">to elements.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:127pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Searching and retrieval of elements</p></td><td style="width:189pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s28" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Searching and retrieval <span class="s6">of elements is</span></p><p class="s28" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">fast <span class="s6">since arraylist provides random access.</span></p></td><td style="width:163pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s28" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Searching and retrieval <span class="s6">of elements is </span>slow <span class="s6">because of</span></p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">sequential access to elements.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:89pt"><td style="width:127pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 16pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Addition and removal of elements</p></td><td style="width:189pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s28" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Adding and removal of elements in random positions is slow<span class="s6">.For example if we want to add element to middle of the list we have to move the elements in the list and then we need to insert the element. Similarly for removing the element we need to follow the same</span></p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">thing.</p></td><td style="width:163pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s28" style="padding-right: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Adding and removal of elements in random positions is fast <span class="s6">because there is no need of resizing the array just by updating the node structures with new addresses.</span></p></td></tr></table><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="225)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Difference between Comparator and Comparable in java?</h2><table style="border-collapse:collapse;margin-left:6.4606pt" cellspacing="0"><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Sno</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-right: 35pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: center;">Comparator</p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s13" style="padding-left: 40pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Comparable</p></td></tr><tr style="height:12pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">1.</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 33pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: center;">Defined in <span class="s28">java.util package</span></p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Defined in <span class="s28">java.lang package.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">2.</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 2pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 11pt;text-align: left;">Comparator interface is used when <span class="s28">we want to compare two different instances</span></p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Comparable is used <span class="s28">to compare itself with other instance</span>.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:45pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">3.</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 2pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Comparator is used when we want <span class="s28">custom sorting</span>.Ex : If we take employee class sorting by</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">employeeId is natural sorting.</p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Comparable is used for <span class="s28">natural sorting </span>of objects.Ex : If we take employee class sorting by ename and age we can say as custom sorting.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">4.</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 2pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Should override <span style=" color: #396;">int compare(T o1, T o2) </span>method which takes two</p><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">instances.</p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Should override <span style=" color: #396;">public int compareTo(T o) </span>method which takes one instance.</p></td></tr><tr style="height:34pt"><td style="width:50pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:2pt;border-left-color:#FFFFFF;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">5.</p></td><td style="width:172pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="padding-right: 2pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For sorting objects <span style=" color: #396;">we use collections.sort(list,new</span></p><p class="s29" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Comparator);</p></td><td style="width:257pt;border-top-style:solid;border-top-width:1pt;border-top-color:#A3A3A3;border-left-style:solid;border-left-width:1pt;border-left-color:#A3A3A3;border-bottom-style:solid;border-bottom-width:1pt;border-bottom-color:#A3A3A3;border-right-style:solid;border-right-width:1pt;border-right-color:#A3A3A3"><p class="s6" style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">For sorting objects <span style=" color: #396;">we use collections.sort(list)</span>;</p></td></tr></table></li><li data-list-text="226)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is concurrent hashmap and its features ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Concurrent HashMap is implemented in <span class="s30">java.util.concurrent </span>package. Concurrent HashMap extends Abstract Map and implements concurrent Map. Concurrent HashMap is used in multi threaded environment.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">]It is similar to Hashtable and synchronized version of hashmap but with minor differences. Concurrent HashMap <span class="s30">does not allow null keys and values</span>.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="227)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 3pt;text-align: left;">Difference between Concurrent HashMap and Hashtable and collections.synchronizedHashMap?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;"><u>Locking Mechansim :</u>ConcurrentHashMap uses completely different hashing mechanism called <span class="s30">lock striping </span>which offers better concurrency and scalability.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">The main advantage of this mechanism is better concurrency instead of synchronizing every method by using common lock which allows only one thread to access at a time, <span class="s30">it allows better concurrency by allowing multiple threads to access</span>.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;"><u>ConcurrentModificationException :</u>ConcurrentHashMap provides iterators which doesnot throw concurrent modification exception which allows only one thread to access iterator, <span class="s30">while synchronized map may throw concurrent modification exception</span>.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="228)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Explain copyOnWriteArrayList and when do we use copyOnWriteArrayList? <span class="p">copyOnWriteArrayList is used in multithreaded environment. If we want to iterate over arraylist ,but the arraylist is updated by other threads to prevent concurrent modification exception we have two solutions :</span></h2><ol id="l89"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">First one is we need to synchronize the list manually by using collections.synchronized(list) and iterate over the list in synchronized block to avoid concurrent modification exception.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">The second one is to use copyOnWriteArrayList which takes care of concurrency.</p><p class="s30" style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">The advantage of using copyOnWriteArrayList is no need to synchronize list explicitly<span class="p">. So when we use copyOnWriteArrayList when a thread modifies the list while the other thread was iterating it does not modify original list but creates a copy of list with modified contents so that the iterator won’t know the modifications made to original list.</span></p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="229)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about fail fast iterators in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">When iterator iterates over collection, collection should not be modified except by that iterator. Modification means collection cannot be modified by thread when other thread is iterating, if such modification happens a concurrent modification exception will be thrown.Such kind of iterators are fail fast iterators.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Ex : ArrayList,HashSet,HashMap. Almost all the iterators implemented in collections framework are fail fast.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="230)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about fail safe iterators in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Fail safe iterators are iterators which does not throw concurrent modification exception, when one thread modifies collection and other thread in the process of iterating the collection.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">It does not throw concurrent modification exception because when other thread was iterating it does not modify original list but creates a copy of list with modified contents so that the iterator won’t know the modifications made to original list.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">Ex : copyOnWriteArrayList</p><p class="s12" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Core java Serialization interview questions</p></li><li data-list-text="231)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is serialization in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">Serialization is the process of converting an object in to bytes, so that it can be transmitted over the network,or stored in a flat file and can be recreated later. Serialized object is an object represented as sequence of bytes that includes objects data, object type, and the types of data stored in the object.</p></li><li data-list-text="232)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is the main purpose of serialization in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">The main uses of serialization are :</p><ol id="l90"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Persistence:</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can write data to a file or database and can be used later by deserializing it.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Communication :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">To pass an object over network by making remote procedure call.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">Copying :</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">We can create duplicates of original object by using byte array.</p></li><li data-list-text="4)"><p style="padding-left: 35pt;text-indent: -28pt;text-align: left;">To distribute objects across different JVMs.</p></li></ol><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="233)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What are alternatives to java serialization?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">XML based data transfer JSON based data transfer.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">XML based data transfer : We can use JIBX or JAXB where we can marshall our object’s data to xml and transfer data and then unmarshall and convert to object.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 10pt;text-align: left;">JSON based transfer : We can use json to transfer data.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="234)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Explain about serializable interface in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">To implement serialization in java there is an interface defined in java.io package called serializable interface. Java.io.Serializable interface is an marker interface which doesnot contain any any methods. A class implements Serializable lets the JVM know that the instances of the class can be serialized.</p><p class="s14" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Syntax:</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">public interface Serializable {</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">}</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="235)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">How to make object serializable in java?</h2><ol id="l91"><li data-list-text="1)"><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Our class must implement serializable interface.If our object contains other objects those class must also implement serializable interface.</p></li><li data-list-text="2)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">We use ObjectOutputStream which extends OutputStream used to write objects to a stream.</p></li><li data-list-text="3)"><p style="padding-left: 19pt;text-indent: -12pt;text-align: left;">We use ObjectInputStream which extends InputStream used to read objects from stream</p></li></ol></li><li data-list-text="236)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What is serial version UID and its importance in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">Serial version unique identifier is a 64 bit long value .This 64 bit long value is a hash code of the class name,super interfaces and member. Suid is a unique id no two classes will have same suid. Whenever an object is serialized suid value will also serialize with it.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">When an object is read using ObjectInputStream, the suid is also read. If the loaded class suid does not match with suid read from object stream, readObject throws an InvalidClassException.</p></li><li data-list-text="237)"><h2 style="padding-top: 3pt;padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">What happens if we don’t define serial version UID ?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If we don’t define serial version UID JVM will create one suid for us. But it is recommended to have suid rather than JVM creating because at run time JVM has to compute the hashcode of all the properties of class. This process makes serialization low. We can’t serialize static fields one exception to this is suid where suid gets serialized along with the object.</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">Ex :private static final long serialVersionUID = -5885568094444284875L;</p><p style="padding-top: 1pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="238)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">Can we serialize static variables in java?</h2><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 107%;text-align: left;">We can’t serialize static variables in java. The reason being static variable are class variables that belongs to a class not to object, but serialization mechanism saves only the object state not the class state.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="239)"><h2 style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">When we serialize an object does the serialization mechanism saves its references too? <span class="p">When we serialize an object even the object it refers must implement serializable then the reference objects also get serialized. If we don’t make reference objects serializable then we get NotSerializableException.</span></h2><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p></li><li data-list-text="240)"><h2 style="padding-left: 33pt;text-indent: -27pt;text-align: left;">If we don’t want some of the fields not to serialize How to do that?</h2></li></ol><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;line-height: 106%;text-align: left;">If we don’t want to serialize some fields during serialization we declare those variables as transient. During deserialization transient variables are initialized with default values for primitives and null for object references.</p><p style="text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><br/></p><p class="s31" style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;">More questions and answers</p><p style="padding-left: 6pt;text-indent: 0pt;text-align: left;"><a href="http://becomejavasenior.com/blog/2015/07/01/327-interview-questions-java-developer/">http://becomejavasenior.com/blog/2015/07/01/327-interview-questions-java-developer/</a></p></body></html>
